The test framework polls `openshift_ptp_clock_state{iface=...,process="ptp4l"}` via `getMetric()` in `test/pkg/metrics/metrics.go:235`. For `ens2f0np0`, the interface role metric shows SLAVE (ptp4l parsed the port-state-change log in `processParsedEvent`, `log_parsing.go:168`), but the `openshift_ptp_clock_state` metric is absent because `updateClockStateMetrics()` (called at `log_parsing.go:94`) is only invoked when ptp4l emits an **offset measurement** line — meaning ptp4l entered SLAVE state but never produced a sync/offset measurement. `ens2f3np3` never left LISTENING, indicating ptp4l received no Announce/Sync from a master on that port. Cross-suite evidence (TGM failures: `Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM` stuck at 248; `error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded` on GM pod) confirms the grandmaster node (cnfdf32) was itself not LOCKED, so downstream followers on cnfdf31 had no valid master to synchronize to. Root Cause Groups: - ~33/38 failures — BC `ptp4l` stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248), `ens2f0np0` never transitioning to SLAVE: The dualnicbc suite's boundary clock does not lock to the grandmaster. This is the dominant failure mode across the dualnicbc suite.

--- ## Cross-Suite CI Failure Summary **Job:** `periodic-ci-openshift-release-main-nightly-5.0-e2e-telco5g-ptp` **Version:** 5.0 | **Total failures:** 38 | **Suites:** dualnicbc, tbc, all --- **TL;DR:** Two `main`-branch regressions — a broken `pmc` invocation and new T-BC hardware constraints — plus a cascading BC FREERUN condition account for all 38 failures. --- **Root Cause Groups:** - **~33/38 failures — BC `ptp4l` stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248), `ens2f0np0` never transitioning to SLAVE:** The dualnicbc suite's boundary clock does not lock to the grandmaster. This cascades into every downstream test that depends on a locked BC: sync verification, metric presence, clock-class event checks, recovery tests, and phc2sys restart tests. This is the dominant failure mode across the dualnicbc suite. - **3/38 failures — `pmc` CLI invocation bug (commit `3b93c9f`, Jun 9 2026):** `getClockIDViaPMC()` in `test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go` passes `GET` and `PARENT_DATA_SET` as separate positional CLI arguments. The `pmc` binary rejects both tokens as `bad command`, so clock-ID lookups always fail, causing `Eventually` blocks in sync tests to time out deterministically. Affects: "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority". - **2/38 failures — T-BC topology solver finds no valid solution on lab cluster (PR #205, merged 2026-06-23):** The new `TelcoBoundaryClock` test scenario (introduced on `main` only) requires at least one node with a WPC NIC (Intel E810/E830) satisfying a 5-step constraint chain. Nodes cnfdf30/31/32 do not satisfy these constraints, so `BeforeAll` fails with `no T-BC solution found for TBC` after all three retries, aborting both the `tbc` serial suite and the `all` parallel suite's `SynchronizedBeforeSuite`. --- **Cross-Suite Patterns:** | Root Cause | dualnicbc | tbc | all | |---|---|---|---| | BC FREERUN cascade (clock class 248) | Yes (dominant) | No | No | | `pmc` CLI invocation bug (`3b93c9f`) | Yes (3 tests) | No | No | | T-BC hardware topology miss (PR #205) | No | Yes (suite abort) | Yes (BeforeAll abort) | - The **BC FREERUN** and **`pmc` bug** failures are exclusive to `dualnicbc` — they require a dual-NIC BC hardware topology that the other suites do not exercise. - The **T-BC solver failure** is shared identically between `tbc` and `all`: both abort at setup with the same error string from `testconfig.go:1899`, caused by the same missing WPC-NIC hardware on the same nodes (cnfdf30/31/32). - All three root causes originate from **`main`-branch changes** (test scripts run from `TEST_BRANCH=main` against `release-5.0` images). No production image regression is implicated. --- ** Actionable Recommendations:** 1. **Fix the `pmc` invocation immediately (commit `3b93c9f`):** In `test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go`, change the `ExecCommand` call to pass the management command as a single string argument — `[]string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"}` — or pipe it via stdin. This unblocks 3 deterministic failures with a one-line change and restores the clock-ID fallback path. 2. **Add a hardware-availability guard to the `tbc`/`all` `BeforeAll`:** Replace the `Fail()` call when `solutions["TBC"]` is empty with a `Skip()` so that absence of WPC-NIC hardware causes the suite to be skipped rather than failing the entire describe block. This converts 2 hard failures to expected skips without requiring cluster reprovisioning. Every call to this fallback deterministically fails, causing `Eventually` timeouts in sync tests. Confirmed non-flake — retries all fail identically. --- **Cross-Suite Patterns:** | Root Cause | dualnicbc | tbc | all | |---|---|---|---| | BC FREERUN / no SLAVE lock | ✅ (dominant) | — | — | | PMC invocation bug (3b93c9f) | ✅ | possibly | possibly | | T-BC topology / no WPC NIC | — | ✅ | ✅ | - The **T-BC topology failure is shared across `tbc` and `all`** — the same `PtpConfigTelcoBC()` code path and the same hardware gap produce identical errors in both suites. - The **BC FREERUN and PMC bug are `dualnicbc`-specific** in the evidence available, though the PMC helper is shared code and could surface in other suites if the log-stream fallback is triggered there too. - No failures appear to be genuine flakes — all three root causes are deterministic given current cluster state and current `main` test code. --- ** --- # Per-Suite Details ## dualnicbc --- ### Suite: dualnicbc (11 failures) **Suite TL;DR:** Three tests fail because of a broken `pmc` invocation introduced by a `main`-branch test script commit; the remaining eight failures stem from the BC's `ptp4l` being stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248) with `ens2f0np0` reporting MASTER instead of SLAVE, cascading into event, metric, and recovery test failures. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: PMC command invocation bug in test helper** (affects: "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority") - **Evidence:** ``` parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET grandmasterIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET ``` - **Root Cause:** Commit `3b93c9f` ("tests: add retries to PTP clock ID lookups") introduced `getClockIDViaPMC()` in `test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go` (line 143) as a fallback when log-stream parsing fails. It invokes `pmc` via `pods.ExecCommand` with `[]string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"}` — passing `GET` and `PARENT_DATA_SET` as two separate positional arguments. The `pmc` binary does not accept management commands as CLI arguments; it reads them interactively. Both tokens are rejected as `bad command: GET` / `bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET`, so `re.FindStringSubmatch` never matches and the function always returns an error. This causes the outer `Eventually` in the sync tests to timeout waiting for a clock ID that can never be read. For `os-clock-sync-state-change` events, both DataValues — the `notification` ("LOCKED") and the `metric` (-2) — share the **same** ResourceAddress (`/cluster/node/.../CLOCK_REALTIME`), so the second loop iteration (`metric`) silently overwrites the first (`notification`). The resulting map has no `"notification"` key, so `testSyncState` in `test/conformance/parallel/ptp.go:413–414` always reads `state = ""` and `wasLocked` never becomes `true`. The clock hardware was actually LOCKED (confirmed by the raw CloudEvent data), but the test could not detect it and timed out after 5 minutes per `{Enable:true FailureThreshold:1 Duration:5}` config. --- **TL;DR:** A test-code key collision in `createStoredEvent` (commit `d20ffcbf0c`, 2026-07-03) causes every "PTP Slave Clock Sync" event test to miss the LOCKED state and time out. --- **Root Cause Groups:** - **15/15 failures: Key collision in `createStoredEvent` silently drops LOCKED notification state, causing all PTP Slave Clock Sync tests to time out** — commit `d20ffcbf0c` on `k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator` main (merged 2026-07-03) changed the `StoredEventValues` map key from `v.DataType` to `v.Resource` (ResourceAddress). For `os-clock-sync-state-change` events, both the `notification` ("LOCKED") and `metric` (-2) DataValues share the same ResourceAddress (`/cluster/node/.../CLOCK_REALTIME`), so the metric entry silently overwrites the notification entry. `ptp.go:414` then reads `values["notification"]` as `""` (key absent), `wasLocked` never becomes `true`, and the test times out after 5 minutes. The clock hardware was confirmed LOCKED in raw CloudEvent data — this is a **test-code regression only**; production `release-4.22` images are unaffected. --- **Cross-Suite Patterns:** - **All suites share the same root cause** (`bc`, `oc`, and per the oc analysis also `dualfollower`, `dualnicbc`, `dualnicbcha`). The failure is systematic and code-level: every suite running `Event based tests PTP Slave Clock Sync` hits the same bad key lookup path in `testSyncState`. No suite-specific variation is present — the `clockOffset=0.000000` debug output (instead of the expected metric value) appears in both analyzed suites identically, confirming the key-mismatch affects both the `notification` and `metric` reads. --- **Actionable Recommendations:** 1. **Revert the map key change in `createStoredEvent`** (`test/pkg/event/event.go`, v2 path, ~line 730): restore `v.DataType` as the key for each DataValue loop iteration, undoing the `d20ffcbf0c` change. This directly fixes all 15 failures across every suite. 2. **Add a regression test for `createStoredEvent`** that asserts the returned map contains both `"notification"` and `"metric"` keys when given a dual-DataValue `os-clock-sync-state-change` event — preventing future key changes from silently breaking event parsing. 3. **Block the PR that introduced `d20ffcbf0c`** (or open a revert PR) against `k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator` main immediately, as every nightly run on this job will continue to fail 100% of the time until the fix lands. --- **Overall Issue Class:** `test_regression` **Overall Severity:** HIGH — all 15 test failures trace to a single deterministic code regression on main; no hardware or infra issues involved, but the entire nightly job is broken on every run until resolved. --- # Per-Suite Details ## bc --- ### Suite: bc (1 failures) **Suite TL;DR:** The single bc-parallel test "PTP Slave Clock Sync" timed out unable to detect a LOCKED OS clock because a test-code change in `k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator` commit `d20ffcbf0c` (July 3, 2026) introduced a key collision bug in `createStoredEvent` that silently drops the notification state from received CloudEvents. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: Key collision in `createStoredEvent` drops LOCKED notification state** (affects: `[It] [bc-parallel] Event based tests PTP Slave Clock Sync`) - **Evidence:** ``` [event.go: 730] Context Attributes, type: event.sync.sync-status.os-clock-sync-state-change source: /sync/sync-status/os-clock-sync-state Data, {"version":"1.0","values":[ {"ResourceAddress":"/cluster/node/cnfdf32.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com/CLOCK_REALTIME","data_type":"notification","value_type":"enumeration","value":"LOCKED"}, {"ResourceAddress":"/cluster/node/cnfdf32.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com/CLOCK_REALTIME","data_type":"metric","value_type":"decimal64.3","value":"-2"} ]} [event.go: 734] Latency for the event: 36942 ms [ptp.go: 411] got map[eventsource:/sync/sync-status/os-clock-sync-state ... eventvalues:map[/cluster/node/cnfdf32.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com/CLOCK_REALTIME:-2]] [ptp.go: 419] clockOffset=0.000000 [ptp.go: 393] [FAILED] OS Clock was never LOCKED and test timed out ``` - **Root Cause:** Commit `d20ffcbf0c` on `k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator` (merged 2026-07-03, title: "CNF-19588: CI test for clockClass recovery after cloud-event-proxy crash") changed `createStoredEvent` in `test/pkg/event/event.go` (v2 path, line 730) to use `v.Resource` (ResourceAddress) as the `StoredEventValues` map key instead of `v.DataType`. For `os-clock-sync-state-change` events, both DataValues — the `notification` ("LOCKED") and the `metric` (-2) — share the **same** ResourceAddress (`/cluster/node/.../CLOCK_REALTIME`), so the second loop iteration (`metric`) silently overwrites the first (`notification`). The resulting map has no `"notification"` key, so `testSyncState` in `test/conformance/parallel/ptp.go:413–414` always reads `state = ""` and `wasLocked` never becomes `true`. The clock hardware was actually LOCKED (confirmed by the raw CloudEvent data), but the test could not detect it and timed out after 5 minutes per `{Enable:true FailureThreshold:1 Duration:5}` config. This is a **test-code regression on main** — the production `release-4.22` images are unaffected. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** `d20ffcbf0c` on `k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator` main (2026-07-03) — https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/d20ffcbf0c - **Is it a flake?** No — the key collision is deterministic and will fail on every run until fixed. - **Suggested Fix:** In `test/pkg/event/event.go` `createStoredEvent` v2 path, restore `v.DataType` as the map key for each DataValue (reverting the key change from `d20ffcbf0c`). To also support the multiple-`metric` BC clock-class use case that motivated the change, either accumulate values into a slice or use a composite key like `"<ResourceAddress>/<DataType>"` and update all callers that read `values["notification"]` and `values["metric"]` accordingly. **Suite Issue Class:** test_regression **Suite Severity:** HIGH ## oc --- ### Suite: oc (1 failures) **Suite TL;DR:** The single `[oc-parallel] Event based tests PTP Slave Clock Sync` test timed out because the OS clock LOCKED state event was received but its values were keyed by `ResourceAddress` (e.g. `/cluster/node/cnfdf30.../CLOCK_REALTIME:15`) instead of by `DataType` (`"notification"`), so `ptp.go:414` never resolved `state == "LOCKED"` and `wasLocked` remained `false` until the 5-minute timeout fired. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: Event value key mismatch — OS clock LOCKED state never recognized** (affects: `[It] [oc-parallel] Event based tests PTP Slave Clock Sync`) - **Evidence:** ``` [FAILED] OS Clock was never LOCKED and test timed out In [It] at: /tmp/cnf-s7FwM/ptp-operator-conformance-test/test/conformance/parallel/ptp.go:393 @ 07/12/26 11:01:22.395 ``` ``` DEBUG [ptp.go: 411] got map[eventsource:/sync/sync-status/os-clock-sync-state eventtimestamp:2026-07-12 10:55:50.49315292 +0000 UTC eventtype:event.sync.sync-status.os-clock-sync-state-change eventvalues:map[/cluster/node/cnfdf30.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com/CLOCK_REALTIME:15]] DEBUG [ptp.go: 419] clockOffset=0.000000 ``` ``` INFO [event.go: 734] Latency for the event: 36928 ms INFO [event.go: 589] received term signal, exiting MonitorPodLogsRegex ``` The `SynchronizedBeforeSuite` also shows: `PtpEventsIsConsumerReady= false` at start, confirming the consumer app was only ready after the 1-minute `BeforeEach` warmup. - **Root Cause:** `testSyncState` in `test/conformance/parallel/ptp.go` subscribes to `OsClockSyncStateChange` events and calls `event.PushInitialEvent` to get the current clock state. The initial event IS received (a stale LOCKED event timestamped 37 seconds earlier), but its `StoredEventValues` map uses the `ResourceAddress` path (`/cluster/node/cnfdf30.../CLOCK_REA

Full analysis
--- **TL;DR:** A single test-code timeout regression blocks clock-sync validation in 20/22 tests; 2 remaining failures expose a known DPLL holdover gap. --- **Root Cause Groups:** - **20/22 failures — `GetProfileLogID` log-stream snapshot times out (test regression, commit `41f3dd9`):** Suites bc (3), dualfollower (3), dualnicbc (3), dualnicbcha (3), oc (2), tbc (6). Commit `41f3dd9bf0b33f642d931eb005e54eba89b337fa` ("address gemini review", Feb 26 2026) silently reduced the `GetPodLogsRegex` snapshot context from `TimeoutIn3Minutes` to `TimeoutIn1Minute`. By the time any suite runs (the `linuxptp-daemon` has been up for 3–5 hours), the container's accumulated log volume cannot be streamed within 1 minute; `io.ReadAll` returns `context deadline exceeded`. The fallback follow-stream also fails because the `Ptp4lConf: #profile:` marker was written only at daemon startup and does not reappear. All six affected suites produce the same `GetProfileLogID attempt N failed … error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded / timedout waiting for matches` chain before exhausting the 202-second test deadline. The tbc suite (6 failures) has a compounding factor: `linuxptp-daemon-t68bh` on `cnfdf32` is also crash-looping (suspected duplicate `DiscoveredFollowerInterfaces=[ens7f0 ens7f0]` config), which kills active streams mid-read and amplifies the timeout. - **2/22 failures — DPLL holdover collapses to FREERUN (class 248) without sustaining class 7 (known tech debt):** Suite tgm (2). In `linuxptp-daemon/pkg/dpll/dpll.go:656`, the `DPLL_HOLDOVER` branch immediately checks `!d.inSpec`; if `inSpec` was cleared during the preceding `DPLL_FREERUN` transition, the daemon fires `holdoverCloseCh` and falls to class 248 without ever holding class 7. The code carries an explicit `// TODO: GNSS holdover currently doesn't offer holdover out of spec` comment. Both TGM holdover tests fail deterministically on `cnfdf32`. --- **Cross-Suite Patterns:** | Root Cause | Suites affected | Suite-specific? | |---|---|---| | `GetProfileLogID` 1-min timeout regression | bc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, oc, tbc | No — all 6 suites hit identical error path | | tbc crash-loop on `cnfdf32` (compounding) | tbc only | Yes — specific to T-BC node config | | DPLL holdover tech debt | tgm only | Yes — only holdover tests exercise this path | All suites share the identical `ptptesthelper.go:71` → `ptphelper.go:123` → `pods.go:220` call chain. The `oc` suite provided the most complete trace, isolating `41f3dd9` as the breaking commit. The `dualnicbc` per-suite analysis incorrectly attributed the cause to hardware/GM unavailability; the actual mechanism is the same log-stream timeout seen everywhere else. --- **Actionable Recommendations:** 1. **Revert or fix commit `41f3dd9` in `GetPodLogsRegex` (highest impact — fixes 20/22 failures):** In `test/pkg/pods/pods.go` (around line 220), restore the snapshot context timeout from `TimeoutIn1Minute` back to `TimeoutIn3Minutes` (as set by the prior commit `9c1bc7f`). Alternatively, redesign `GetProfileLogID` to search only the log tail (e.g., `sinceSeconds` or `tailLines` parameter on the Kubernetes log request) rather than re-reading the full accumulated log, making the lookup O(recent output) regardless of daemon uptime. 2. **Investigate and fix the `linuxptp-daemon` crash-loop on `cnfdf32` (fixes tbc amplification):** The `DiscoveredFollowerInterfaces=[ens7f0 ens7f0]` duplicate entry in the T-BC config suggests a profile-discovery bug where the same interface is registered twice. Confirm whether `test-wpc-tbc` profile configuration is correct for node `cnfdf32.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com`, and fix the `tbc-tr`/`tbc-tt` interface mapping to prevent the crash-loop that makes log-stream reads impossible even with a corrected timeout. 3. **Address the DPLL holdover tech debt in `linuxptp-daemon/pkg/dpll/dpll.go:656` (fixes tgm failures):** Implement the deferred holdover-in-spec window so that after GNSS loss the daemon sustains `ClockClass7` for the holdover duration before falling to class 248, mirroring the T-BC holdover behavior called out in the existing `TODO` comment. --- **Overall Issue Class:** `test_regression` (dominant — 20/22 failures caused by `41f3dd9` test-code change; tgm failures are `test_failure` against known gap; tbc crash-loop is `infra_other`) **Overall Severity:** HIGH — a single test-code commit broke clock-sync verification across every PTP topology for the entire job, producing 20 false-negative failures that mask any real regressions in the 4.21 PTP stack. --- # Per-Suite Details ## bc --- ### Suite: bc (3 failures) **Suite TL;DR:** All three ClockSync tests fail identically because `GetProfileLogID` cannot find the `Ptp4lConf: #profile:` log entry in the `linuxptp-daemon` pod's log stream, causing the master-clock-ID lookup to time out before sync can be verified. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: Profile log-ID lookup failure — regex mismatch/log rollover** (affects: all 3 failed tests) - **Evidence:** - Test 1 (`Slave can sync to master`, ptpconfig `test-bc-master1`): ``` [FAILED] Timed out after 202.066s. `GetProfileLogID` (`ptphelper.go:69`) uses the regex `(?m).*?Ptp4lConf: #profile: %s(.|\n)*?message_tag \[(.*)\]`. This pattern is only logged by `printNodeProfile` (`daemon.go:893`) when `nodeProfile.Ptp4lConf` already contains the RENDERED config (i.e., after `*configInput = configOutput` at `daemon.go:1119` has updated the pointer's string on a PREVIOUS apply). **TL;DR:** 13 of 15 failures are a single test flake — a log-rotation race that voids `GetProfileLogID`; 2 are a WPC T-GM holdover hardware failure. --- **Root Cause Groups:** - **13/15 failures — `GetProfileLogID` log-rotation timeout (bc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, oc):** `BasicClockSyncCheck` → `GetClockIDForeign` → `GetProfileLogID` (ptphelper.go:69) opens a `Follow: true` log stream and searches for `(?m).*?Ptp4lConf: #profile: <name>(.|\n)*?message_tag \[.*\]`. That regex only matches a line emitted once by `printNodeProfile` at daemon startup. Cluster setup finished at ~02:06; ClockSync tests ran at ~04:00–06:00 (~2–4 h later). By then CRI-O log rotation had cycled the startup entry out of the K8s-served log buffer. The snapshot read yields nothing (~26 s); the follow-stream times out after 180 s — producing the observed ~206–218 s failure duration across every suite. The "Can provide a profile with higher priority" variant adds ~60–90 s of profile-apply wait before hitting the same timeout (yielding ~287–298 s). - **2/15 failures — WPC T-GM DPLL holdover not sustained (tgm):** After GNSS disconnect, ts2phc either never emits the `"holdover"` log token (test 1 — 3+ min of retries, class stays at 6) or emits class-7 followed 7 ms later by class-248 (test 2 — DPLL flips through holdover and drops to FREERUN before the test can assert it). Root is in the WPC DPLL firmware or the `ts2phc_parser.go:162-163` holdover-detection logic, not in the test itself. --- **Cross-Suite Patterns:** | Suite | Failures | Root Cause | |---|---|---| | bc | 3 | Log rotation (GetProfileLogID) | | dualfollower | 3 | Log rotation (GetProfileLogID) | | dualnicbc | 3 | Log rotation (GetProfileLogID) | | dualnicbcha | 2 | Log rotation (GetProfileLogID) — same 206–218 s signature | | oc | 2 | Log rotation (GetProfileLogID) — same 206–218 s signature | | tgm | 2 | WPC T-GM holdover hardware/firmware failure | All five non-tgm suites share an identical root cause and near-identical failure durations. The dualnicbcha and oc per-suite analyses characterize the symptom as "LOCKED state timeout," but the timing signature (206–218 s, 287–298 s) and the `GetProfileLogID` call stack are identical to bc/dualfollower/dualnicbc. tgm is the only suite with a distinct, hardware-level root cause. --- **Actionable Recommendations:** 1. **Fix `GetProfileLogID` to not depend on rotated startup logs.** Instead of parsing the one-shot `printNodeProfile` startup line, query the current PTP configuration state directly — either from a `/metrics` endpoint, the `PtpConfig` CR status, or by triggering a daemon profile-reload (e.g., a no-op annotation update) immediately before the test assertion window. This single fix eliminates 13/15 failures. 2. **Investigate the WPC DPLL holdover firmware behavior on `cnfdf32.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com`.** Capture `ts2phc` raw log output during GNSS disconnect to determine whether the DPLL hardware never enters holdover or enters and exits it within milliseconds. If the latter, check whether the DPLL holdover duration register is being set correctly from `ts2phc.holdover` config and whether a firmware update is available for the WPC card. 3. **Add a canary assertion for daemon log reachability before ClockSync tests.** A short pre-check that confirms `GetPodLogsRegex` can read at least one log line from the daemon container (not the specific startup pattern) would convert a silent 206 s timeout into a fast, labeled skip/infra-failure, making future regressions easier to triage. --- **Overall Issue Class:** `test_flake` (13/15); `infra_other` (2/15 tgm) **Overall Severity:** MEDIUM — the dominant failure mode is a pre-existing, deterministic time-dependent flake (not a code regression); the tgm failures indicate a real hardware/firmware problem on one lab node but affect only 2 tests. --- # Per-Suite Details ## bc --- ### Suite: bc (3 failures) **Suite TL;DR:** All 3 bc ClockSync tests fail at the same step — `GetProfileLogID` cannot find the regex `Ptp4lConf: #profile: <name>...message_tag [...]` in the linuxptp-daemon container logs, because this log pattern only appears on a second profile application and the daemon had been stable for ~2 hours since cluster setup with no re-apply. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: `GetProfileLogID` regex never matches — daemon log pattern requires second profile apply** (affects: all 3 tests) - **Evidence:** ``` [Jun 26 04:03:18.197][ptphelper.go: 123] GetProfileLogID attempt 1 failed for test-bc-master1_test-bc-master1: could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-nqmpf container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded, retrying... The underlying issue — that `Ptp4lConf: #profile:` only appears in logs on the 2nd+ apply — has existed as a latent flake since `GetProfileLogID` was introduced. Unknown PR for the original introduction; the relevant release branch is `release-4.21` in `github.com/openshift/ptp-operator`. - **Is it a flake?** Yes — the test passes when something triggers a second profile application between cluster setup and the ClockSync test window (e.g., operator config reconciliation, hardware config event, daemon restart). In this run, ~2 hours of stability after setup meant no re-apply occurred. - **Suggested Fix:** In `GetProfileLogID`, instead of relying on the `Ptp4lConf:` log (which requires a second apply), read the ptp4l config file directly from the pod filesystem (`/var/run/ptp4l.0.config`)

The test helper `GetProfileLogID` in `test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go` opens a live Kubernetes log stream (`Follow: true`, no `TailLines`) via `pods.GetPodLogsRegex` searching for the regex `(?m).*?Ptp4lConf: #profile: <name>(.|\n)*?message_tag \[([^\]]*)\]` within a 3-minute timeout. The stream — opened with `context.TODO()` so no test-side deadline — is being terminated by the infrastructure with `context deadline exceeded` before the regex can be matched. This error pattern repeats identically across all ClockSync tests in bc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, and dualnicbcha suites, confirming a cluster-wide log streaming connectivity issue rather than a daemon log format regression. The `linuxptp-daemon` does emit this log line (`printNodeProfile` in `pkg/daemon/daemon.go:1369` writes the rendered `Ptp4lConf` with `#profile:` prefix and `message_tag`), but the HTTP connection carrying the pod log stream is dropped before the data reaches the test. Full analysis
--- **TL;DR:** linuxptp-daemon `main` PR #617 broke ts2phc PHC-lock and ptp4l metrics, cascading into 31 of 32 failures across all four suites. --- **Root Cause Groups:** - **~19/32 failures — linuxptp-daemon PR #617: ts2phc stuck in FREERUN despite DPLL locked (GM-cascade)** Node `cnfdf32` (WPC T-GM): DPLL hardware reports LOCKED (`state=1`) but ts2phc reports FREERUN (`state=0`). PHC never synchronizes → phc2sys never starts → ptp4l clock class stays 248 → GM never advertises valid Announce messages → BC node `cnfdf32/ens2f0np0` stays in MASTER instead of SLAVE → all downstream BC and slave sync tests fail. Suites: **tgm** (9 tests), **dualnicbc** (~7 tests), **dualnicbcha** (~9 tests, all cascading from this same GM failure) - **3/32 failures — linuxptp-daemon PR #617: `processParsedMetrics` emits `iface="master"` instead of real interface name** New `log_parsing.go` (introduced in PR #617) resolves `ptpMetrics.Iface` via `GetPhcID2IFace("master")` and `GetAlias("master")`, neither of which maps to the real slave interface (`ens2f0np0`). The metric `openshift_ptp_clock_state{iface="master"}` is emitted instead of `{iface="ens2f0np0"}`, so test assertions waiting for the real interface label time out. Suite: **dualfollower** (all 3 tests) - **~3–5/32 failures — ptp-operator commit `3b93c9f`: `getClockIDViaPMC` passes pmc args as separate slice elements** `[]string{..., "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"}` should be `[]string{..., "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"}`. pmc's `pmc_do_command` parses both tokens from one string via `sscanf`; passing them separately produces `bad command: GET` / `bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET`. Triggered as a fallback when the BC is already in FREERUN. Based on the suite analyses in the prompt, here is the cross-suite summary: --- **Job:** `periodic-ci-openshift-release-main-nightly-5.0-e2e-telco5g-ptp-upstream` **Version:** 5.0 | **Total failures:** 38 --- ## TL;DR Two code regressions merged in late June broke metric label lookups and T-BC topology discovery, cascading to 38 failures. --- ## Root Cause Groups - **~36/38 failures — Interface alias mismatch in `openshift_ptp_clock_state` metric labels** (primary driver across dualfollower and likely all remaining suites) Upstream PR #617 (`k8snetworkplumbingwg/linuxptp-daemon`, commit `fd6ff1e`, merged 2026-06-30) introduced `pkg/alias/manager.go`, causing `updateClockStateMetrics()` to emit `iface="ens2fx"` (NIC alias) instead of `iface="ens2f0np0"` (raw interface name). All conformance tests that look up `openshift_ptp_clock_state` by raw interface name now find nothing, producing deterministic `<iface> not found` failures. - **2/38 failures — T-BC topology solver finds no valid WPC NIC configuration** (tbc + all suites) PR #205 (`openshift/ptp-operator`, commit `84723c8`/`aede1e9`, merged 2026-06-23) added `PtpConfigTelcoBC()` with strict solver constraints requiring WPC NICs (Intel E810 with GNSS/PPS) as both T-BC receiver and local grandmaster. The `cnfdf30/31/32` lab hardware satisfies none of these constraints, so `[SynchronizedBeforeSuite]` aborts before any test body runs. --- ## Cross-Suite Patterns | Root cause | dualfollower | tbc | all | Notes | |---|---|---|---|---| | Interface alias mismatch (`fd6ff1e`) | Yes (4 explicit) | Likely | Likely | Pervasive — any test querying `openshift_ptp_clock_state` by raw `iface` label fails | | T-BC topology absent | No | Yes (1) | Yes (1) | Suite-specific to TBC tests; `SynchronizedBeforeSuite` abort means no TBC test can pass regardless | The interface alias regression is cross-suite because `openshift_ptp_clock_state` metric lookups by raw interface name are used throughout ptp-operator conformance tests. The T-BC issue is isolated to suites that exercise the `AlgoTelcoBCString` solver path. --- ## Actionable Recommendations 1. **Fix metric label lookup in ptp-operator tests (unblocks ~36 failures).** In the conformance test helper that queries `openshift_ptp_clock_state`, resolve the slave interface name through the same alias lookup used by the daemon (`alias.GetAliasValue(ifname)`) before comparing metric labels. Alternatively, the linuxptp-daemon can expose both raw and alias labels, or revert the alias-in-metric-label behavior in PR #617 pending a coordinated test update. 2. **Skip T-BC suite gracefully when hardware is absent (unblocks 2 failures).** Change `PtpConfigTelcoBC()` (and the `[SynchronizedBeforeSuite]` that calls it) to emit a Ginkgo `Skip()` rather than a hard `Expect(...).To(BeNil())` error when `solutions["TBC"]` is empty. This prevents a missing hardware topology from failing the entire suite and turning an expected "not applicable" into a false failure. 3. **Gate the T-BC test job on lab hardware capabilities.** Add a pre-flight check (or CI job label) that confirms at least one `cnfdfXX` node has WPC NIC interfaces before running TBC tests, and skip or xfail the job if the hardware inventory is insufficient. --- ## Overall Issue Class `test_regression` ## Overall Severity **HIGH** — Two deterministic regressions introduced within one week of each other account for all 38 failures; no flakes involved. The interface alias change blocks the majority of PTP conformance coverage until tests or daemon are updated. --- # Per-Suite Details ## dualfollower --- ### Suite: dualfollower (4 failures) **Suite TL;DR:** All 4 dualfollower tests fail because a June 30 upstream sync PR introduced interface aliasing in linuxptp-daemon that changes `openshift_ptp_clock_state` metric labels from raw interface names (e.g., `ens2f0np0`) to NIC-level aliases (e.g., `ens2fx`), while the test code still queries raw names. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: Interface alias mismatch in `openshift_ptp_clock_state` metric** (affects: "Slave can sync to master", "Dual follower can sync when one follower port goes down", "Can provide a profile with higher priority") - **Evidence:** ``` no Follower port in expected LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1 (node=cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, label="ptp/clock-under-test", slaveIfs=[ens2f0np0 ens2f3np3]). **TL;DR:** WPC T-GM grandmaster never achieved GNSS lock (class 248), collapsing all 4 suites; pmc argument bug added 5 independent failures. --- **Root Cause Groups:** - **20/25 failures — GM in FREERUN (clock class 248), cascading to all BC/slave/follower sync tests** Affects: tgm (5/5), dualnicbcha (~6/8), dualnicbc (~6/9), dualfollower (3/3). The WPC T-GM node hosting `linuxptp-daemon-7g7z8` never transitioned out of FREERUN during the run. With no locked GM advertising Announce messages, the entire downstream chain — BC → dualnicbc → dualnicbcha → dualfollower slaves — could not lock. The tgm log stream stayed open but hit `context deadline exceeded` after 340 s without ever emitting a LOCKED event; all four state-based tgm tests timed out on `Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM` / `<bool>: false`. The dualfollower node `cnfdf31` exhibits both missing `openshift_ptp_clock_state` metric for `ens2f0np0` and `ens2f3np3` stuck in LISTENING — consistent with no upstream Announce to trigger SLAVE election. - **5/25 failures — pmc invoked with split arguments; `GET PARENT_DATA_SET` rejected as two bad commands** Affects: dualnicbc ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority") and dualnicbcha ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master"). `pmc` is called with `GET` and `PARENT_DATA_SET` as separate argv elements; the binary responds `bad command: GET` / `bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET`. Identical verbatim error appears in both suites, ruling out a flake. Likely triggered by the RHCOS 10.2 pmc binary (linuxptp ≥ 4.3, el10_2) changing batch-mode argument tokenization, or the test helper failing to quote the combined string. Other pmc queries (e.g. `GET DEFAULT_DATA_SET`) still succeed, confirming the socket and ptp4l process are reachable. --- **Cross-Suite Patterns:** | Root Cause | dualfollower | dualnicbc | dualnicbcha | tgm | |---|---|---|---|---| | GM FREERUN / GNSS never locked | All 3 | ~6 | ~6 | All 5 | | pmc split-arg bug | — | 3 | 2 | — | - The GM FREERUN failure is **shared across all 4 suites** — it is the single largest driver and the only failure in tgm and dualfollower. - The pmc split-arg bug is **shared between dualnicbc and dualnicbcha only** (suites that exercise `PARENT_DATA_SET` queries via the BC node). - No failures are genuinely suite-specific; the dualfollower and tgm failures are pure downstream consequences of the shared GM not locking. --- **Actionable Recommendations:** 1. **Re-run the job and inspect GM GNSS hardware first.** Confirm whether the WPC T-GM node achieves GNSS/DPLL lock in a fresh run. This single fix would resolve ~20/25 failures. 2. **Fix pmc invocation to pass `GET PARENT_DATA_SET` as a single quoted argument.** In both the test helper (`ptp-operator-conformance-test`) and any `exec.Command` / shell call in `linuxptp-daemon`, ensure the action+management-ID are passed as one argument string (e.g. `exec.Command("pmc", ..., "GET PARENT_DATA_SET")`), or switch to the interactive `RunPMCExpGetParentDS` path with lowercase command (`"get PARENT_DATA_SET"`) to match the RHCOS 10.2 pmc binary's expected input. This would surface the GNSS issue immediately and save ~30 min of wasted CI time per run. --- **Overall Issue Class:** `test_flake` (dominant: GNSS hardware failure is a known lab environmental flake) + `test_regression` (secondary: pmc argument bug introduced with RHCOS 10.2 / linuxptp upstream sync `0459bc0`) **Overall Severity:** CRITICAL — 25/25 failures, 4/4 suites completely down in a nightly periodic job. --- # Per-Suite Details ## dualfollower --- ### Suite: dualfollower (3 failures) **Suite TL;DR:** All 3 dualfollower ClockSync tests timed out waiting for node `cnfdf31`'s follower interfaces to reach LOCKED state because the `openshift_ptp_clock_state` metric for `ens2f0np0` was never emitted by linuxptp-daemon, and `ens2f3np3` was stuck in LISTENING rather than SLAVE role. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: Slave node never locked — missing clock_state metric and port stuck in LISTENING** (affects: all 3 tests) - **Evidence:** ``` # Tests 1 & 2 — identical error no Follower port in expected LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1 (node=cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, label="ptp/clock-under-test", slaveIfs=[ens2f0np0 ens2f3np3]). This is consistent with a linuxptp version in the `release-5.0` image where the pmc interactive-mode command table does not include `GET` / `SET` prefixes, or with `management_enabled=0` on ptp4l (added in linuxptp ≥4.2 as the default) causing ptp4l to respond with NOT\_SUPPORTED which pmc renders as "bad command". The `Dockerfile.ocp` (`linuxptp-daemon/addons/redhat/Dockerfile.ocp:12`) installs `linuxptp` from RHEL9 repos with no version pin, so an unintended package update to ≥4.2 is a plausible trigger. -

The `release-5.0` linuxptp-daemon publishes `openshift_ptp_clock_state` using an alias computed by `pkg/alias.GetAliasValue()` (`linuxptp-daemon/pkg/utils/utils.go`, regex `^(.+?)(\d+)(?:np\d+)?(\..+)?$`): for `ens2f0np0` and `ens2f3np3` this strips the `npN` suffix and trailing port digit, producing `ens2fx`. The metric is therefore published as `iface="ens2fx"`. The `main`-branch test helper (`test/pkg/metrics/metrics.go:201–222`, commit `f28aceb1`) only tries the raw name (`ens2f0np0`) and a naive last-character alias (`ens2f0npx`); it never tries `ens2fx`. Because `ens2f0np0` and `ens2f3np3` are ports on the same Intel NIC with a single PHC group, the daemon's `calculateAliases` does not fall back to original names (fallback only fires when two distinct PHC IDs share the same alias), so `ens2fx` is the only label emitted. The metric lookup always returns "not found", and each test exhausts its 600 s `Eventually` retry window.

--- ## Cross-Suite Summary — `periodic-ci-openshift-release-main-nightly-5.0-e2e-telco5g-ptp` **TL;DR:** The WPC T-GM never achieved GNSS lock (class 248), wiping 22 tests; 3 more failed from a metric alias bug. --- ### Root Cause Groups - **22/25 failures — T-GM stuck at clock class 248 (FREERUN), GNSS lock never achieved** *(suites: tgm 5, dualnicbc 9, dualnicbcha 8)* The WPC grandmaster (`linuxptp-daemon-vzbr9`) never transitioned to clock class 6 for the entire ~32-minute run. With no locked upstream source, every BC's upstream port (`ens2f0np0`) stayed MASTER (BMCA had nothing better to announce), `pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET` returned `bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET` on all retries, and every downstream sync/event/metric assertion failed. The prime suspect is commit **`9ba6326`** ("CNF-24996: Decouple GNSS and DPLL", merged to `release-5.0` ~Jun 22) which explicitly removes GNSS state from DPLL state calculation in `pkg/dpll/dpll.go` and `pkg/event/event.go` — breaking the ts2phc → DPLL → ptp4l clock-class-6 promotion pathway for WPC hardware. - **3/25 failures — Interface alias mismatch: daemon labels vs. test query** *(suite: dualfollower 3)* The `release-5.0` linuxptp-daemon computes an alias via `pkg/alias.GetAliasValue()` (regex strips `npN` suffix + trailing digit), publishing `openshift_ptp_clock_state` as `iface="ens2fx"`. The `main`-branch test helper (`test/pkg/metrics/metrics.go:201–222`, commit **`f28aceb1`**) only tries the raw name (`ens2f0np0`) and a naive last-char alias (`ens2f0npx`) — never `ens2fx`. Every metric lookup returns "not found" and each test exhausts its 600s `Eventually` window. --- ### Cross-Suite Patterns | Suite | GM FREERUN | Alias mismatch | |---|---|---| | tgm | YES (direct — GM is the SUT) | — | | dualnicbc | YES (cascaded from GM) | — | | dualnicbcha | YES (cascaded from GM) | — | | dualfollower | Contributing (no upstream sync) | YES (primary label) | - **tgm / dualnicbc / dualnicbcha** share a single root cause: the upstream GM not locking. The failure signature is identical across all three (`clockClass=248`, `role=MASTER`, `bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET`). - **dualfollower** is partially unique: its primary reported failure mode is the alias lookup bug (`ens2fx` not found), but the concurrent GM lock failure means the slaves had no valid source to sync to anyway — both issues compound. - No suite-specific infra or build anomalies were identified beyond these two root causes. --- ### Actionable Recommendations 1. **Investigate/revert `9ba6326` on `release-5.0`** — Run `check_backport.py 9ba6326 release-5.0` to confirm the commit is present, then assess whether re-coupling GNSS state into DPLL state calculation (or providing an alternative signal path) restores clock-class-6 promotion on WPC hardware. This single fix resolves 22/25 failures. 2. **Fix the alias lookup in `test/pkg/metrics/metrics.go`** — Replace the naive `npx` alias candidate with logic matching the daemon's `GetAliasValue()` regex (strip `npN` suffix + trailing port digit, e.g. `ens2f0np0` → `ens2fx`). "available op…" truncated in evidence files but the pattern is the same for both slave interfaces `ens2f0np0` and `ens2f3np3`) ``` no Follower port in expected LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1 (node=cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, label="ptp/clock-under-test", slaveIfs=[ens2f0np0 ens2f3np3]) ``` (from `junit-failures.txt`, each test timed out after 600 s) Test scripts run from `main`, images from `release-5.0`: ``` + export TEST_BRANCH=main + export PTP_UNDER_TEST_BRANCH=release-5.0 + export IMG_VERSION=release-5.0 ``` (from `ci-operator-build-log.txt` lines 37–42) - **Root Cause:** The `release-5.0` linuxptp-daemon publishes `openshift_ptp_clock_state` using an alias computed by `pkg/alias.GetAliasValue()` (`linuxptp-daemon/pkg/utils/utils.go`, regex `^(.+?)(\d+)(?:np\d+)?(\..+)?$`): for `ens2f0np0` and `ens2f3np3` this strips the `npN` suffix and trailing port digit, producing `ens2fx`. The metric is therefore published as `iface="ens2fx"`. The `main`-branch test helper (`test/pkg/metrics/metrics.go:201–222`, commit `f28aceb1`) only tries the raw name (`ens2f0np0`) and a naive last-character alias (`ens2f0npx`); it never tries `ens2fx`. Because `ens2f0np0` and `ens2f3np3` are ports on the same Intel NIC with a single PHC group, the daemon's `calculateAliases` does not fall back to original names (fallback only fires when two distinct PHC IDs share the same alias), so `ens2fx` is the only label emitted. The metric lookup always returns "not found", and each test exhausts its 600 s `Eventually` retry window. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** Commit `f28aceb1` ("Make getMetic to check for ifname and alias", merged via PR #193, March 11 2026) is the most recent change touching this logic. It partially improved the fallback but introduced an incorrect alias candidate (`ens2f0npx` instead of `ens2fx`). The underlying incompatibility (daemon aliasing vs. test aliasing) was latent before this PR; that PR did not cherry-pick to `release-5.0`. The daemon-side alias feature in linuxptp-daemon `release-5.0` (`pkg/alias/manager.go::calculateAliases`, `pkg/utils/utils.go::GetAliasValue`) pre-dates this run and is present in the current `release-5.0` build. - **Is it a flake?** No — deterministic regression; the alias mismatch will reproduce on every run with this hardware and these branches. - **Suggested Fix:** In `test/pkg/metrics/metrics.go::getMetric()`, add `GetAliasValue(aIf)` (imported from `linuxptp-daemon/pkg/utils` or reimplemented with the same regex) as a third candidate in `ifCandidates` so the test uses the same aliasing logic as the daemon. The one-liner fix: `ifCandidates = append(ifCandidates, utils.GetAliasValue(aIf))` after the existing `ens2f0npx` candidate. This must be done on `main` and then backported to any release branch that uses the same test runner. **Suite Issue Class:** `test_regression` **Suite Severity:** HIGH ## dualnicbc --- ### Suite: dualnicbc (9 failures) **Suite TL;DR:** All 9 failures trace back to the T-GM (Grandmaster) never reaching clock class 6 (LOCKED) — clock class stays at 248 (FREE_RUN) across every node — so the BC has no valid master to sync from, causing every downstream sync, event, and metric assertion to fail. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: BC cannot sync — GM and BC both stuck at clock c

`getClockIDViaPMC` in `test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go:144` invokes pmc via `pods.ExecCommand` with the command split as two separate argv entries: `[]string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"}`. The linuxptp `pmc` binary treats every non-option argument as an independent command token; it processes `"GET"` as a standalone command (returning "bad command: GET") then `"PARENT_DATA_SET"` as another (returning "bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET"). The fix is to pass the command as a single string: `"GET PARENT_DATA_SET"`. This fallback path is only triggered when log-based clock-ID parsing fails; with the BC not locked (Group 2), logs never contain `"selected best master clock"`, so this pmc fallback is always exercised. -

--- ## Cross-Suite Summary: `periodic-ci-openshift-release-main-nightly-4.19-e2e-telco5g-ptp` **Job:** `periodic-ci-openshift-release-main-nightly-4.19-e2e-telco5g-ptp` **Version:** 4.19 | **Total Failures:** 22 --- **TL;DR:** 22 failures from three independent causes: cluster API server collapse, a linuxptp-daemon log-format mismatch, and a GNSS simulation code regression. --- **Root Cause Groups:** - **13/22 failures — Cluster API server VIP instability (`10.8.34.117:6443`):** - `bc` suite (11): 1 TCP i/o timeout on API VIP → 10 cascading `Unauthorized` failures as the kubeconfig bearer token expired ~2.5–3 h into the run with no reachable API server to refresh it. - `dualnicbcha` suite (2): log-stream connections to the same VIP terminated with `context deadline exceeded` when the cluster was still degraded. - All post-test artifact collectors (must-gather, `oc get` steps) also fully `Unauthorized`, confirming cluster-wide auth collapse by the end of the run. - **7/22 failures — `release-4.19` linuxptp-daemon missing `Ptp4lConf: #profile:` log / `/var/run` config header:** - `dualfollower` suite (3) and `dualnicbc` suite (4): `GetProfileLogID` exhausted its full ~202 s retry budget (`timedout waiting for matches`) for every tested profile name (`test-bc-master1`, `test-slave1`, `temp`). The `/var/run/ptp4l.*.config` fallback also failed, meaning the `release-4.19` daemon never wrote or logged the `#profile: <name>` header that the `main`-branch test framework requires. The `release-4.19` nightly image (cut `2026-06-25`) may have diverged from `main`'s `daemon.go:printNodeProfile()` or `config.go:RenderPtp4lConf()` behavior. - **2/22 failures — TGM GNSS simulation code regression (commit `7c915d9`, `main` branch):** - `tgm` suite (2): Commit `7c915d9` ("Replace ublox coldboot with config…") swapped out `ubxtool -p COLDBOOT` for `CFG-NAVSPG-INFIL_NCNOTHRS,50,1`. The u-blox module in time-only mode continues generating 1PPS even without a GNSS fix, so the Intel E810 DPLL never loses its reference and never enters HOLDOVER. Result: ClockClass 248 (FREERUN) instead of ClockClass 7 (HOLDOVER) — both tests fail (`Timed out waiting for clock class 7`; `expected metric [7.000000] but got 248`). --- **Cross-Suite Patterns:** | Root Cause | Suites Affected | Suite-Specific? | |---|---|---| | API server VIP instability | `bc`, `dualnicbcha` | No — same VIP `10.8.34.117:6443`, same run | | `#profile:` log/file missing (release-4.19 daemon) | `dualfollower`, `dualnicbc` | No — identical error string, different pods/nodes | | GNSS simulation regression (`7c915d9`) | `tgm` only | Yes — WPC T-GM hardware path only | - `dualfollower` and `dualnicbc` share an identical failure mode (stream alive, regex never matches) pointing to a `main`-test vs. `release-4.19`-daemon compatibility break. - `dualnicbcha`'s `context deadline exceeded` differs from `dualfollower`/`dualnicbc`'s `timedout waiting for matches`: the stream connection itself died (API instability), not just an absent log line — placing `dualnicbcha` in the infra group. - `bc` is the worst-hit suite but all 11 failures are infrastructure-cascade, not PTP logic. - `tgm` is fully independent of the other suites; its failures would reproduce on a healthy cluster. --- **Actionable Recommendations:** 1. **Revert `7c915d9` on `main` (fixes 2 tgm failures, unblocks holdover testing):** Restore `ubxtool -p COLDBOOT` (or use the `ubxtool -p RESET` / `ubxtool -z CFG-TP-TIMEPULSE0_ENA,0` approach) to actually cut 1PPS output to the DPLL. `CFG-NAVSPG-INFIL_NCNOTHRS` does not interrupt the hardware clock reference and cannot reliably trigger DPLL HOLDOVER on E810-based T-GM hardware. 2. **Investigate and remediate the API server VIP `10.8.34.117:6443` (fixes 13 failures if cluster is healthy on retry):** Examine the cluster event log for `2026-06-30 ~07:31 UTC` — specifically keepalived/haproxy VIP failover, control-plane node restarts, or etcd leader elections. The entire `bc` suite and `dualnicbcha` suite will pass on a stable cluster. If the cluster is transient CI infra, re-run the job; if it is a persistent lab cluster, file a hardware/infra ticket. 3. **Audit `release-4.19` linuxptp-daemon for `#profile:` emission (fixes 7 failures):** Diff `pkg/daemon/daemon.go` and `pkg/daemon/config.go` between `main` and `release-4.19` around `printNodeProfile()` (line ~819 in `release-4.19`) and `RenderPtp4lConf()` (config.go:437). If the `release-4.19` image no longer prepends `#profile: <name>` to rendered configs or no longer calls `printNodeProfile()` after config write, either backport the log statement to `release-4.19` or add a fallback detection path in the `main` test framework that does not depend on that header. --- **Overall Issue Class:** `infra_timeout` (dominant, 13/22) with a compounding `test_regression` (`7c915d9`, 2/22) and a probable `test_failure` / version-skew incompatibility (7/22) **Overall Severity:** CRITICAL — the entire job failed; root causes span infra instability, a committed code regression on `main`, and a potential `main`/`release-4.19` daemon compatibility break affecting 3 of 5 suites. --- # Per-Suite Details ## bc --- ### Suite: bc (11 failures) **Suite TL;DR:** The bc suite failed entirely due to infrastructure-level API server access loss mid-run — one test hit a TCP-level timeout reaching the cluster API VIP, and all 10 subsequent tests hit `Unauthorized` after the kubeconfig bearer token expired ~2.5–3 hours into the 3-hour job. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: API server VIP unreachable (TCP i/o timeout)** (affects: `PTP ClockSync Slave can sync to master`) - **Evidence:** ``` finding pod for test-bc-master1_test-bc-master1: Get "https://10.8.34.117:6443/api/v1/namespaces/openshift-ptp/pods?labelSelector=app%3Dlinuxptp-daemon": dial tcp 10.8.34.117:6443: i/o timeout ``` The test timed out after 617.575s. **TL;DR:** API server instability and a large linuxptp-daemon vendor sync (PR #613, merged 2026-06-23) together caused all 26 failures across 5 suites. --- **Root Cause Groups:** - **8/26 — API server credential expiry + TCP unreachability (bc suite only):** 7 tests hit `Unauthorized` (kubeconfig credentials expired mid-run); 1 hit `dial tcp 10.8.34.117:6443: i/o timeout`; 1 cascaded to a suite-level timeout. - **7/26 — linuxptp-daemon log stream never matched profile regex (bc, dualfollower, dualnicbcha):** `GetProfileLogID` / `GetForeignClockID` waited ~200–205 s for `Ptp4lConf: #profile: … message_tag` in the live log stream and got `context deadline exceeded`. The linuxptp-daemon pods never (re-)emitted the profile line, indicating the daemon (post-PR #613) does not re-log profiles on profile re-application as the tests expect. - **6/26 — ptp4l.1 stuck in FREERUN, clockClass 248, never locked to GM (dualnicbc):** `GetClockClassViaPMC` consistently returned 248 instead of 6; the BC port re-elected itself MASTER after a bounce instead of recovering to SLAVE; cloud-event-proxy received no LOCKED events; PTP metrics were absent. The new `tBCTransitionCheck()` logic in the overhauled `pkg/daemon/daemon.go` (introduced in PR #613) is the primary suspect. - **2/26 — T-GM fails to enter holdover (clockClass 248 instead of 7) after GNSS loss (tgm):** `DpllConfig.stateDecision()` never enters the `DPLL_HOLDOVER` branch; `getWorseState()` collapses a mixed HOLDOVER/FREERUN DPLL phase+frequency reading to FREERUN, so the event handler emits clockClass 248 instead of 7. Both tests see a deterministic wrong value, not a timing race. - **2/26 — PMC command-format regression breaking BC master identity lookup (dualnicbc):** `finding pod for test-grandmaster: no PTP pods found for label="ptp/test-grandmaster"` — the new socket-based `pmc.go` introduced in PR #613 produces a command that the PMC binary does not parse, returning no output and leaving the grandmaster lookup empty. --- **Cross-Suite Patterns:** | Pattern | bc | dualfollower | dualnicbc | dualnicbcha | tgm | |---|---|---|---|---|---| | Log stream timeout (context deadline exceeded) | 2 | 3 | — | 2 | — | | API credential expiry / TCP unreachable | 8 | — | — | — | — | | clockClass 248 FREERUN (wrong state) | — | — | 6 | — | 2 | | PMC command regression | — | — | 2 | — | — | - **Shared across bc + dualfollower + dualnicbcha:** Log stream `context deadline exceeded` — the linuxptp-daemon DaemonSet pods (`linuxptp-daemon-4gvkl`, `-qh745`, `-lrzfg`, `-fgzlj`, `-24cbs`) all fail to emit the expected profile log line. Different code paths but both trace back to the daemon's state-machine logic altered in PR #613. - **Suite-specific:** API credential expiry is bc-only (likely a timing accident of which suite ran longest/first). PMC command regression is dualnicbc-only. T-GM holdover is tgm-only. - **Common upstream trigger:** `linuxptp-daemon` PR #613 / commit `0459bc0` ("CNF-24996, OCPBUGS-90708: Sync from upstream 22-Jun-2026", merged 2026-06-23) — a 5,947-file vendor sync that overhauled `pkg/daemon/daemon.go`, introduced `pkg/daemon/pmc.go`, and rewrote T-BC transition logic — is the strongest candidate for the majority of failures (Groups 2–5 above, covering ~17/26 tests). --- **Actionable Recommendations:** 1. **Revert or bisect linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (commit `0459bc0`).** It is the single most recent change to the daemon and plausibly breaks: profile log emission (17 tests across 3 suites), T-BC lock detection (6 tests in dualnicbc), DPLL holdover state resolution (2 tests in tgm), and PMC command formatting (2 tests in dualnicbc). --- **TL;DR:** 11/13 failures are a test/daemon version mismatch; 2/13 are a T-GM hardware holdover regression. --- **Root Cause Groups:** - **11/13 failures — `Ptp4lConf: #profile:` log line absent from `release-4.20` daemon** (bc: 3, dualfollower: 3, dualnicbc: 3, dualnicbcha: 2) The test helper `GetProfileLogID` (test code running from `main`) searches for a log regex (`Ptp4lConf: #profile: <name>`) that is only emitted after `*configInput = configOutput` + `printNodeProfile` — code introduced in linuxptp-daemon `main` PR #617 (commit `fd6ff1e`, merged 2026-06-30) and **not backported to `release-4.20`**. The CI job deploys `release-4.20` daemon images (`USE_UPSTREAM=false`), so the pattern is never logged. `GetProfileLogID`'s internal 3-minute deadline consumes the entire outer `Eventually` window, leaving the `/var/run` fallback no time to run. All failures surface as either `timedout waiting for matches` (stream alive, pattern never appeared) or `context deadline exceeded` (Kubernetes log-stream dropped), with a secondary cluster-API `Unauthorized` state observed post-run in dualnicbc/dualnicbcha, consistent with infrastructure stress from 11 concurrent 200-second stream-read timeouts. - **2/13 failures — T-GM DPLL does not enter holdover on GNSS disruption** (tgm: 2) When GNSS signal is lost or rebooted on WPC T-GM hardware, the Intel DPLL is expected to transition to `lockStatus: holdover` (clock class 7). Instead, the DPLL stays in or falls directly to `FREERUN` (clock class 248), so `openshift_ptp_clock_class` never reaches 7. Both tgm tests fail: one by timeout polling for clock class 7, one by direct metric assertion finding 248. This is independent of the log-line issue; the `release-4.20` daemon or underlying firmware may have a regression in holdover state management. --- **Cross-Suite Patterns:** | Root Cause | Suites Affected | Failures | |---|---|---| | `#profile:` log line missing from `release-4.20` daemon | bc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha | 11 | | T-GM DPLL does not enter holdover (clock class 7) | tgm | 2 | The 11-failure group is fully cross-suite: all four PTP topology suites hit identical pod-log-stream errors on six different pods across different nodes, ruling out any single pod, node, or suite-specific cause. The tgm failures are completely isolated to hardware GNSS/holdover behavior and share no mechanism with the other 11. --- **Actionable Recommendations:** 1. **Backport linuxptp-daemon `main` PR #617 to `release-4.20`** (fixes 11/13 failures). The commit `fd6ff1e` adds `*configInput = configOutput` and the unconditional `printNodeProfile` call that emits `Ptp4lConf: #profile:` into daemon logs. Without this, any `main` test branch that relies on `GetProfileLogID` will always time out against `release-4.20` images. Alternatively, gate the test's log-search path on daemon version and immediately fall through to the `/var/run` exec-based fallback instead of waiting a full 3 minutes first. 2. **Investigate T-GM DPLL holdover regression on `release-4.20`** (fixes 2/13 failures). Audit recent commits to `linuxptp-daemon/release-4.20` and `cloud-event-proxy/release-4.20` for changes in `pkg/event/event.go` DPLL state-transition logic. Also verify WPC hardware firmware version matches the expected holdover capability; if firmware is the variable, pin firmware version in the CI telco5g cluster. 3. **Extend the outer `Eventually` timeout in `BasicClockSyncCheck`** or make the `/var/run` fallback the *first* path (not the last resort). The current design serially exhausts a 3-minute log-stream deadline before trying a fast exec-based config read, meaning any transient log-streaming disruption (or version mismatch) guarantees test failure regardless of actual PTP sync state. --- **Overall Issue Class:** `test_regression` (The dominant failure mode — 11/13 — is caused by `main` test code depending on a daemon log line that exists only in `main`, not in the `release-4.20` images the job is actually testing. The tgm pair is `test_failure` / potential daemon regression, but does not change the overall classification.) **Overall Severity:** HIGH (11/13 failures are systemic and reproducible across every topology suite in every run that pairs `main` test scripts with `release-4.20` daemon images; the job cannot pass in this configuration without the backport or a test-side workaround.) --- # Per-Suite Details ## bc --- ### Suite: bc (3 failures) **Suite TL;DR:** All 3 BC ClockSync tests time out because `GetProfileLogID` cannot find the `Ptp4lConf: #profile:` log pattern in the `release-4.20` linuxptp-daemon container, and the `/var/run` fallback is exhausted within the 3-minute `Eventually` window. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: `GetProfileLogID` log pattern absent from `release-4.20` linuxptp-daemon** (affects: all 3 tests — "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority") - **Evidence:** ``` could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-g59s2 container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded ``` ``` could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-7khz9 container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded ``` ``` could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-g59s2 container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=timedout waiting for matches ``` The same error occurs across **all four suites** (bc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha) on different pods (`-g59s2`, `-7khz9`, `-68lc9`, `-d75dq`), confirming a daemon-wide, systematic failure. - **Root Cause:** `GetClockIDForeign` (called from `BasicClockSyncCheck` in `test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go:66`) first calls `GetProfileLogID` (`test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go:84`), which searches for the regex `(?m).*?Ptp4lConf: #profile: <name>(.|\n)*?message_tag \[(.*)\]` in the `linuxptp-daemon-container` logs. Per branch-awareness policy, a `main`-only change cannot be the root cause; the true underlying issue is that the `main` test code (`GetProfileLogID`, introduced in ptp-operator commit `73a75ec`, March 25 2026) was written assuming a log-output behavior that exists only on `main` linuxptp-daemon, not in `release-4.20` images. Full analysis
**TL;DR:** The CI job's build/deploy pipeline never installed ptp-operator, wiping out 13 tests before they started; 4 remaining failures are linuxptp-daemon behavioral regressions. --- **Root Cause Groups:** - **13/17 failures — ptp-operator never deployed to cluster (bc suite, all 13 bc-serial tests)** The `telco5g-ptp-tests` step wiped and re-created the `openshift-ptp` namespace, launched a privileged podman pod to build ptp-operator, linuxptp-daemon, and cloud-event-proxy from their upstream `main` branches, but the build log is truncated at line 496 (mid-template-substitution). The step ran for ~1h46m and the operator never appeared — no Deployment, no Pods, no `PtpOperatorConfig` CR. Every bc-serial test aborted within milliseconds of start (`NotFound` on `ptpoperatorconfigs`, `deployments/ptp-operator`, and ptp-operator pods). - **2/17 failures — DPLL holdover not maintained on T-GM node `cnfdf32` (tgm suite)** Test 1: GNSS coldboot never pushes DPLL out of `DPLL_LOCKED`; ClockClass stays at 6, never reaches 7. Test 2: DPLL does briefly enter holdover (ClockClass 7) but immediately exits to FREERUN/ClockClass 248 because `linuxptp-daemon/pkg/dpll/dpll.go:658` maps `!d.inSpec` directly to `PTP_FREERUN`, bypassing sustained holdover.   • 4.22-e2e-telco5g-ptp-upstream (2026-07-06)
The conformance tests open a Kubernetes log stream to the `linuxptp-daemon-container` and look for ptp4l lines containing the foreign-clock-ID (the grandmaster clock identity that ptp4l emits once it reaches SLAVE state, e.g. `FOREIGN_MASTER_RECORD_SET` or similar). When ptp4l is NOT synchronized — because the upstream PTP grandmaster is unavailable or the sync chain broke — those log lines are never produced and the test times out. The fact that every ClockSync test on every suite failed simultaneously against multiple different pods on multiple nodes points to a cluster-wide PTP environment failure (grandmaster or uplink down), not an isolated daemon crash. Configuration/API tests in the same suite (operator deployment, lease, namespace) all passed, confirming the daemon pods were running; only the PTP-sync-dependent tests failed.
Full analysis
**TL;DR:** T-GM GNSS lock loss (ClockClass 248/Freerun) collapsed the entire PTP sync chain, causing all 14 failures across all 5 suites. --- **Root Cause Groups:** - **12/14 failures — T-GM GNSS unlocked (ClockClass 248), cascading to all BC/slave ClockSync tests** (suites: bc ×3, dualfollower ×3, dualnicbc ×3, dualnicbcha ×2, tgm ×2): The WPC T-GM node in `telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com` lost GNSS lock and, critically, failed to enter holdover (ClockClass 7) — instead transitioning directly to Freerun (ClockClass 248). This is confirmed directly by the tgm suite ("expected a metric [7.000000] but got map[metric:248]", "Timed out waiting for clock class 7") and is the upstream cause of all ClockSync timeouts in every other suite: without a GNSS-locked grandmaster, ptp4l on BC/slave nodes never reaches SLAVE state and the `GetForeignClockID` log-stream helper never matches its regex, firing the 202-second timeout on every test. The same `could not get any profile line / could not find regex in log stream` error message appears across 6 different daemon pods (`jvf75`, `9ssfb`, `z7mfj`, `lkhnx`, `s8frf`, `cklkh`, `h4bbm`) on multiple nodes. - **1/14 failures — Prometheus not returning valid responses during CPU Utilization test** (suite: bc ×1): The parallel CPU Utilization test in `bc` failed because Prometheus was returning no valid data. This is a secondary symptom of the same cluster-health degradation: a lab with a broken PTP grandmaster and, in some suites, API server credential expiry (`Unauthorized` at `07:53:36Z`) is consistent with a broader cluster instability window on 2026-07-03. - **Contributing factor (not a separate root cause) — Kubernetes API server degradation mid-run**: Some suites saw `error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded` (dualnicbcha ×2) rather than the log-stream `timedout waiting for matches` pattern (bc, dualfollower, dualnicbc). The API server also emitted `Unauthorized` errors at job teardown. This is a compounding instability but does not change the root cause — the PTP tests would have failed regardless due to the absent grandmaster signal. --- **Cross-Suite Patterns:** | Suite | Failures | Root cause | Suite-specific? | |---|---|---|---| | bc | 3 ClockSync + 1 CPU-util | GNSS loss (ClockSync); Prometheus degraded (CPU-util) | No — shared GNSS root | | dualfollower | 3 ClockSync | GNSS loss | No | | dualnicbc | 3 ClockSync | GNSS loss (most direct confirmation via tgm cross-reference) | No | | dualnicbcha | 2 ClockSync | GNSS loss + API server dropping streams | No | | tgm | 2 holdover/event tests | GNSS loss / DPLL not entering holdover | Primary source — not cascading from another suite | All 5 suites share a single upstream root cause. No failure is suite-specific. The tgm suite is the causal origin (DPLL hardware or GNSS disable behavior); all other suites are downstream victims. --- **Actionable Recommendations:** 1. **Immediately: Verify and restore GNSS lock on the T-GM node.** SSH to the `cnfdf30/cnfdf31/cnfdf32.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com` T-GM node, check `linuxptp-daemon` logs for GNSS lock status, and confirm the DPLL reports ClockClass 7 before re-triggering the nightly job. Check GNSS antenna connectivity and signal health (GPS signal availability at the lab site). 2. **Investigate DPLL holdover behavior on GNSS loss.** The tgm evidence shows the WPC NIC's DPLL transitions directly from LOCKED → FREERUN (ClockClass 248) without an intermediate HOLDOVER (ClockClass 7) period. This may be caused by the `ubxtool CFG-NAVSPG-INFIL_NCNOTHRS=50` test-disabling mechanism producing an abrupt GNSS cutoff, or the hardware DPLL holdover timeout being shorter than the test's 3-minute polling window. Verify the holdover duration configuration on the WPC NIC and consider whether the test should wait longer or use a softer GNSS-disable method. 3. **Investigate API server token TTL relative to job duration.** The job runs for ~2h50m and the API server was issuing `Unauthorized` errors at teardown. If the CI kubeconfig token has a TTL shorter than the job duration, all long-running nightly jobs will degrade. Rotate or extend the credential lifetime in the `telco5gran` lab CI configuration. --- **Overall Issue Class:** `infra_other` (hardware GNSS failure in the test lab, not a code regression or transient flake) **Overall Severity:** HIGH — 14/14 failures in a nightly periodic job, all suites impacted, no code changes implicated. The job is completely blocked until GNSS lock is restored, but there is no OCP 4.20 code defect to fix. --- # Per-Suite Details ## bc --- ### Suite: bc (4 failures) **Suite TL;DR:** All 3 ClockSync serial tests timed out unable to read the foreign-clock-ID from `linuxptp-daemon-container` pod logs, and the parallel CPU Utilization test failed because Prometheus was not returning valid responses — both symptoms of a systemic infrastructure failure on the test cluster on 2026-07-03. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: linuxptp-daemon log stream returns no foreign-clock-ID output** (affects: "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority") - **Evidence:** ``` could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-jvf75 container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-9ssfb container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-jvf75 container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=timedout waiting for matches ``` All three failures occur against different daemon pods (`jvf75` for test-bc-master1/temp, `9ssfb` for test-slave1), confirming the problem spans multiple nodes. Inspection of the pre-OCPBUGS-95610 release-4.20 source (`3c31e2f`) shows that this commit adds `tBCTransitionCheck` only in the `!stdoutToSocket` branch (lines 1059-1082 of daemon.go) — the path taken when the cloud-event-proxy (CEP) sidecar is absent. The CI job deploys CEP (`SIDECAR_IMG=...cloud-event-proxy:4.20`), so `stdoutToSocket=true` and the `!stdoutToSocket` block is bypassed entirely. OCPBUGS-95610 is therefore not in the hot path for this job and is ruled out as the cause of these failures. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** Unknown — no code change found on `release-4.20` that would affect the `stdoutToSocket=true` (with-CEP) ptp4l sync path. Full analysis
--- **TL;DR:** Nine clock-sync tests fail due to log-stream unavailability; two tgm holdover tests fail due to a bad GNSS-disable method introduced in commit `7c915d9`. --- **Root Cause Groups:** - **9/11 failures — PTP daemon log stream unavailable** (dualfollower ×3, dualnicbcha ×2, dualnicbc ×3 implied): Two overlapping sub-causes produce identical `could not find regex in log stream` errors: - *Sub-cause A (dualfollower, likely dualnicbc):* `GetProfileLogID` searches for a one-time startup log line (`Ptp4lConf: #profile: test-slave1`) that has been rotated out of the container log buffer. With `logReduce: false` and `ptp4l` emitting ~16 summary lines/s plus phc2sys at another ~16/s (~6.4 KB/s), the 10 MiB OCP container log limit is exhausted in ≈26 minutes. The test suite ran ≈38 minutes after cluster setup, so the entry is gone before any test starts. - *Sub-cause B (dualnicbcha, likely contributing to dualnicbc):* PTP sync was never established on the hardware (no Grand Master lock → no `master offset` output), compounded by transient Kubernetes API `Unauthorized` errors that dropped the log-streaming connection mid-run (`context deadline exceeded` variant). - Both variants manifest as: first test gets `context deadline exceeded` (Pass 2 stream times out after 3 minutes), later tests get `timedout waiting for matches`. - **1/11 failure — Prometheus unreachable** (dualnicbcha, CPU-utilization test): The test node could not reach the Prometheus endpoint during the CPU-utilization assertion; this is consistent with the broader environment/auth degradation seen in the same run. - **2/11 failures — WPC T-GM DPLL enters FREERUN (class 248) instead of HOLDOVER (class 7)** (tgm ×2): `disableGNSSViaSignalRequirements()` uses `ubxtool CFG-NAVSPG-INFIL_NCNOTHRS,50` to block the navigation solution, but this leaves the DPLL's physical 1PPS reference intact. The DPLL therefore skips HOLDOVER and drops directly to FREERUN (clock class 248). This replaced a reliable coldboot method (`ubxtool -p COLDBOOT`) in commit `7c915d9` (`Replace ublox coldboot with config for min required signal strength`, Nov 17 2025, `main`). --- **Cross-Suite Patterns:** | Suite | Log-stream failure | Prometheus failure | DPLL FREERUN | |---|---|---|---| | dualfollower | ✓ (3/3, log rotation) | — | — | | dualnicbc | ✓ (3/3, implied) | — | — | | dualnicbcha | ✓ (2/3, stream silent + auth) | ✓ (1/3) | — | | tgm | — | — | ✓ (2/2) | - All three clock-sync suites share the same `could not find regex in log stream` failure signature; only the mechanism differs (log rotation vs. PTP sync never established). - The auth/connectivity degradation (`Unauthorized` errors, dropped streams) is cross-suite infrastructure and likely explains why dualnicbc and dualnicbcha also see stream failures even if the startup line itself was present. - The tgm failures are entirely independent — a test-code regression specific to GNSS-disable logic. --- **Actionable Recommendations:** 1. **Fix log-rotation race (highest impact — unblocks 6–9 failures):** Stop relying on the daemon's one-time startup log line as a test anchor. Either: (a) persist the profile-ID in a Kubernetes ConfigMap or annotation that the test reads via the API, or (b) restart the relevant linuxptp-daemon pod at the start of each suite to guarantee the startup entry is fresh. As a stopgap, set `logReduce: true` in the test PtpConfig to reduce log volume from ~32 lines/s to near-zero background noise, extending log retention beyond the test window. 2. **Restore reliable GNSS disable for T-GM holdover tests (fixes 2 failures):** Revert `7c915d9` or replace `CFG-NAVSPG-INFIL_NCNOTHRS` with a method that actually forces DPLL into HOLDOVER — e.g., restore the `ubxtool -p COLDBOOT` approach or physically disconnect/reconnect the antenna cable in the hardware lab setup. 3. **Investigate and fix environment/auth instability (reduces flakiness):** The `Unauthorized` / `couldn't get current server API group list` errors from the CI operator indicate the cluster's API server credentials expired or the network degraded mid-run. Renew service-account tokens with a longer TTL, or add a pre-test credential-refresh step, to prevent the log-streaming API from being cut off during active tests. --- **Overall Issue Class:** `infra_other` (majority) + `test_regression` (tgm) The 9 log-stream failures are driven by a combination of a fragile test design (relying on ephemeral startup logs) and environment degradation; the 2 tgm failures are a clear test-code regression. **Overall Severity:** HIGH Nine of eleven failures are likely to recur on every run that starts more than ~26 minutes after cluster bring-up, making the suite effectively non-functional in its current state. --- # Per-Suite Details ## dualfollower --- ### Suite: dualfollower (3 failures) **Suite TL;DR:** All 3 clock-sync tests time out because the linuxptp-daemon's startup configuration log entry (`Ptp4lConf: #profile: test-slave1`) has been rotated out of the Kubernetes container log buffer before the tests attempt to read it, making the critical `GetProfileLogID` regex search permanently fail. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: Daemon startup log unavailable due to container log rotation** (affects: "Slave can sync to master", "Dual follower can sync when one follower port goes down", "Can provide a profile with higher priority") - **Evidence:** ``` could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-5c2rz container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded ``` ``` could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-5c2rz container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=timedout waiting for matches ``` From `junit-failures.txt` and from all 3 dualfollower tests (identical pod `linuxptp-daemon-5c2rz`). Each is an invalid standalone command; ptp4l returns `bad command` for each. - **Root Cause:** The `getClockIDViaPMC` function introduced in ptp-operator commit `f291b157` (June 16, 2026 "cleanup: remove dead code, consolidate duplicates") calls `pods.ExecCommand(..., []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"})` — passing `GET` and `PARENT_DATA_SET` as two separate args instead of a single `"GET PARENT_DATA_SET"` string. The pmc tool treats each non-option argument as a separate command token. The underlying reason the PMC fallback is reached at all is that ptp4l hasn't synced (no "selected best master clock" in logs), likely because the upstream GM is also not locked (see TGM failures below). - **Breaking PR/Commit:** https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/f291b157 (June 16, 2026) - **Source File:** https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go (function `getClockIDViaPMC`, ~line 133) - **Is it a flake?** No — the argument-split bug is deterministic in any run using this ptp-operator commit. - **Suggested Fix:** Change `[]string{"pmc", ..., "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"}` to `[]string{"pmc", ..., "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"}` so pmc receives the command as a single argument string.
