--- ## Cross-Suite Summary — `periodic-ci-openshift-release-main-nightly-5.0-e2e-telco5g-ptp` **TL;DR:** The WPC T-GM never achieved GNSS lock (clock class 248 throughout), cascading all 25 failures across every suite. --- **Root Cause Groups:** - **20/25 failures — GM stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248), cascading to all downstream sync assertions** All tgm (5), all dualfollower (3), and the majority of dualnicbc (≥6) and dualnicbcha (≥6) failures trace back to the WPC T-GM pod `linuxptp-daemon-7g7z8` never advancing ts2phc/ptp4l to clock class 6 (GNSS LOCKED). With no locked grandmaster, every BC and slave node remained in LISTENING or FREERUN, causing 600-second `Eventually` timeouts on clock-state metrics that linuxptp-daemon only publishes after a port exits LISTENING state. The overall job also hit the 3h45m CI wall-clock timeout. - **5/25 failures — pmc `GET PARENT_DATA_SET` argument-splitting bug in conformance test helper** Three dualnicbc tests ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority") and two dualnicbcha tests ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master") failed with `bad command: GET` / `bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET`. The pmc binary received the two-word command as two separate argv tokens and rejected each. This is an independent code regression in the ptp-operator conformance test helper's pmc invocation path — it would cause failures even if the GM were locked. --- **Cross-Suite Patterns:** | Root Cause | dualfollower | dualnicbc | dualnicbcha | tgm | |---|---|---|---|---| | GM FREERUN (clock class 248) | All 3 | ~6/9 | ~6/8 | All 5 | | pmc arg-split bug | — | 3/9 | 2/8 | — | - The GM FREERUN pattern is fully cross-suite — every suite has at least one failure directly asserting `Expected <int>: 248 to equal <int>: 6`. Full analysis
--- **Job:** `periodic-ci-openshift-release-main-nightly-4.21-e2e-telco5g-ptp` **Version:** 4.21 | **Total failures:** 15 --- ## Cross-Suite Summary **TL;DR:** A `linuxptp-daemon` regression blocks all slave sync-state detection, timing out 13/15 ClockSync tests across every suite. --- ### Root Cause Groups - **13/15 failures — `GetProfileLogID` / log-stream timeout blocking ClockSync verification** (suites: bc ×3, dualfollower ×3, dualnicbc ×3, dualnicbcha ×2, oc ×2) Every "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", and "Can provide a profile with higher priority" test hits the same ~207–210 s timeout. Two overlapping mechanisms contribute: 1. **`liveGate` startup drain (dualfollower / all slave suites):** The new `liveGate` mechanism in `linuxptp-daemon/pkg/daemon/daemon.go` blocks the socket-writer goroutine for up to 60 s after each profile apply and then *discards* buffered ptp4l lines. `EmitClockSyncLogs()` only replays state for T-GM nodes, so slave/follower sync-state is invisible to the test framework until a fresh live line arrives — which never happens within the `GetProfileLogID` 3-minute window. 2. **Pod log stream closed with `context deadline exceeded` (~60–70 s, dualnicbc / bc):** The `Follow: true` Kubernetes log stream is cut by network infrastructure (HAProxy / kube-apiserver ~60 s idle timeout in OCP 4.21 nightly), causing both retry passes of `GetProfileLogID` to fail before the `Eventually` expires. Both mechanisms trace to the same upstream sync merged the day before the run (linuxptp-daemon PR #613, commit `0459bc0`, Jun 23 2026). - **2/15 failures — WPC T-GM DPLL never sustains clock-class 7 holdover on GNSS loss** (suite: tgm ×2) In both TGM holdover tests, the DPLL on `cnfdf32` either never reaches class 7 (Test 1: 47+ retries, 197 s timeout) or exits class-7 immediately to class 248/FREERUN (Test 2). Root cause is an overly aggressive `maxInSpecOffset` (20 ns) in `HardwareConfig`, causing the in-spec holdover timer to collapse to ~192 s and the DPLL to transition directly to FREERUN before the test verifies it. This is isolated to the tgm suite and the WPC NIC hardware on that node. --- ### Cross-Suite Patterns | Suite | Failures | Root Cause | |---|---|---| | bc | 3/3 | `GetProfileLogID` timeout (operator-pod-deletion restarts daemon mid-test) | | dualfollower | 3/3 | `liveGate` drains buffered lines; slave state invisible | | dualnicbc | 3/3 | Log stream closed `context deadline exceeded` at ~60–70 s | | dualnicbcha | 2/2 | Same systemic ClockSync timeout (no XML artifact captured) | | tgm | 2/2 | **Suite-specific:** DPLL holdover hardware/config regression | **Shared:** bc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha all share the same underlying cause — the `linuxptp-daemon` `liveGate`/stream regression introduced in PR #613 prevents `GetProfileLogID` from ever receiving the `Ptp4lConf: #profile:` startup log within its timeout window. **Suite-specific:** tgm failures are independent — caused by a `HardwareConfig` holdover parameter misconfiguration (or a DPLL driver regression) on the WPC NIC node; they would persist even if the ClockSync stream issue were fixed. --- ### Actionable Recommendations 1. **Revert or fix linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (`0459bc0`, Jun 23 2026).** The `liveGate` drain-on-reset behavior discards the `Ptp4lConf:` startup lines that `GetProfileLogID` depends on. Either: (a) emit a synthetic replay line for slave/follower profiles (matching what `EmitClockSyncLogs` does for T-GM), or (b) gate the drain only on a confirmed-live line rather than discarding all buffered lines on profile apply. This alone unblocks 13/15 failures. 2. **Fix the pod log stream `context deadline exceeded` disconnects.** `GetPodLogsRegex` should reconnect and resume scanning on stream error rather than propagating the error up through `GetProfileLogID`. Adding retry-with-reconnect inside `findRegexInStream` would make the test resilient to the ~60 s kube-apiserver/HAProxy connection timeout independently of the `liveGate` fix. 3. **Investigate the WPC T-GM DPLL holdover configuration.** Audit `holdoverParameters.maxInSpecOffset` in the deployed `HardwareConfig` for `cnfdf32`; a value of 20 ns causes the in-spec timer to expire almost immediately. Align it with realistic oscillator specs (e.g., ≥100 ns) or audit the `linuxptp-daemon/pkg/dpll/dpll.go` holdover-timer formula for a regression introduced alongside PR #613. --- **Overall Issue Class:** `test_regression` **Overall Severity:** CRITICAL — 13/15 ClockSync tests fail across every non-tgm suite due to a single code change merged the previous day; the entire periodic 4.21 PTP job is effectively non-functional. --- # Per-Suite Details ## bc Now I have enough to write the complete analysis. **Cross-Suite CI Failure Summary** **Job:** `periodic-ci-openshift-release-main-nightly-4.20-e2e-telco5g-ptp` **Version:** 4.20 | **Total failures:** 24/24 --- **TL;DR:** `linuxptp-daemon` PR #613 (merged 2026-06-23) silenced container-log output, crashing log-scraping across 5 suites; API credential expiry collapsed the OC suite entirely. --- **Root Cause Groups:** - **12/24 failures — linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (`upstream-sync-2026-06-22`, merged 2026-06-23) broke container-log output** *(bc: 3, dualfollower: 3, dualnicbc: 3, dualnicbcha: 2, oc: 1)* - PR #613 introduced two simultaneous regressions: 1. **Log routing change:** When `LOGS_TO_SOCKET=true` (set because `EnableEventPublisher=true` in all test clusters), `processWithParser()` feeds ptp4l output to the cloud-event-proxy socket and returns early — ptp4l/phc2sys lines never reach container stdout. The test XML confirms `Original EnableEventPublisher value: true`. 2. **Log format change:** The new `printNodeProfile()` function logs the raw `nodeProfile.Ptp4lConf` field, which for test-generated configs starts with `[global]`, not `#profile: <name>`. The `GetProfileLogID` regex (`Ptp4lConf: #profile: <name>(.|\n)*?message_tag \[…\]`) therefore never matches even if logs were reachable. - Both changes cause `GetProfileLogID` (3-minute timeout) to find nothing and error with `could not find regex in log stream … context deadline exceeded` or `timedout waiting for matches`. Every ClockSync test in bc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, and dualnicbcha hits this path. The oc suite's earliest failure is identical before the auth collapse begins. - **10/24 failures — Kubernetes API server credentials expired mid-run** *(oc: 10)* - The kubeconfig token mounted at `/tmp/secret/kubeconfig` expired (or the kube-apiserver VIP `10.8.34.117:6443` was briefly unreachable) during the OC suite's 3598-second window. All 10 tests fail at the first API call with `Unauthorized`; one test reports `connection refused`. Post-suite gather steps (`gather-must-gather`, `gather-extra`, `gather-audit-logs`) all independently fail with `Unauthorized`, confirming cluster-wide credential invalidation, not a test-code issue. - **2/24 failures — T-GM hardware does not enter holdover (clock class 7) after GNSS loss** *(tgm: 2)* - Both WPC T-GM holdover tests observe clock class 248 (FREERUN) throughout, never class 7 (HOLDOVER). The DPLL state machine either bypasses `DPLL_HOLDOVER` and goes directly to `DPLL_FREERUN` on GNSS loss, or `d.inSpec` is false, both of which force the class-248 path. The identical outcome for both cable-pull and GNSS-power-cycle tests in the same run suggests a systematic hardware state issue rather than a race, but a re-run is needed to distinguish a regression from a transient hardware condition. --- **Cross-Suite Patterns:** | Root Cause | bc | dualfollower | dualnicbc | dualnicbcha | oc | tgm | |---|---|---|---|---|---|---| | PR #613 log routing / format regression | 3 | 3 | 3 | 2 | 1 | — | | API credential expiry | — | — | — | — | 10 | — | | T-GM holdover hardware failure | — | — | — | — | — | 2 | - **bc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha** share a single root cause (PR #613) and are not independently broken — fixing PR #613's log-routing behavior would likely unblock all four suites simultaneously. - **oc** is partially affected by PR #613 (1 test) but dominated by credential expiry (10 tests) — a separate infrastructure problem. - **tgm** is entirely isolated: its failures are hardware/DPLL-state dependent and unrelated to the log-routing regression. --- **Actionable Recommendations:** 1. **Revert or patch linuxptp-daemon PR #613's log routing change (fixes 12 failures).** The test framework reads container logs via `kubectl logs`; when `LOGS_TO_SOCKET=true`, ptp4l output is silenced from that stream. The `Ptp4lConf: #profile:` entry is only logged by `printNodeProfile` at daemon startup (`daemon.go:1369`) when `applyNodePtpProfile` writes the config file. After 3.5 hours of `ptp4l` logging at ~1 Hz (offset, master offset, clock state lines), this initial profile-dump entry has either been evicted from the Kubernetes 10 MB pod log buffer or the follow stream never re-emits it — so neither pass of `GetPodLogsRegex` finds the anchor, causing the 3-minute timeout and the `could not get any profile line` error. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** Unknown — no single commit broke this; the log-eviction condition is a latent fragility. The new `PortEngine`-based implementation requires `SKIP_INTERFACES`, which the old implementation did not. On this telco bare-metal setup (cnfdf30/cnfdf31/cnfdf32), the skipped interface is a PTP slave NIC, preventing full outage simulation. - **Source File:** [`test/conformance/serial/ptp.go` L2121–L2190](https://github.com/openshift/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go#L2121-L2190) - **Is it a flake?** No — deterministic failure on this hardware. The `SKIP_INTERFACES` value on this cluster always includes ptp4l.0.config's upstream NIC, so the full outage is never achieved and the test always times out. - **Suggested Fix:** Update the CI step configuration (or node annotation) so `SKIP_INTERFACES` only lists the true management/bond interface, not a PTP slave NIC. Alternatively, configure one of the PTP slave NICs to use a separate physical interface that is not part of the cluster management path. --- **TL;DR:** Dual NIC BC outage test timed out because `SKIP_INTERFACES` protected ptp4l.0.config's slave NIC, leaving one PTP path alive. **Relation Between Failures:** There is only one failing test. PR #611 (`OCPBUGS-88512: Sync from upstream (16-Jun-2026)`, merged 2026-06-16) introduced a new parser framework in `linuxptp-daemon`. The new `processParsedMetrics` in `pkg/daemon/log_parsing.go` omits the "master" → slave-interface-alias resolution that exists in the old `extractRegularMetrics` (`pkg/daemon/metrics.go:457`). When ptp4l logs `master offset -1 s2 freq -3972 path delay 89`, the regex captures `Interface="master"`, and the new code publishes `openshift_ptp_clock_state{iface="master"}` instead of `openshift_ptp_clock_state{iface="ens2f3np3"}`. The test polls for `iface="ens2f3np3"` for the full 10-minute Eventually window before timing out. -

The CI builder base image `registry.ci.openshift.org/ocp/builder:rhel-9-golang-1.22-openshift-4.18` was unavailable (`manifest unknown`) in registry.ci.openshift.org at build time (~20:50 UTC Jun 18). This caused `make docker-build` to fail with exit 125 and the ptp-operator image was never pushed to the internal registry. A secondary bug in the build script — `set +xe` disables exit-on-error to hide registry credentials in logs, but only `set -x` is restored afterward (not `set -e`), so the build failure is silently swallowed and the pod exits 0. However, the ptp-operator controller never completed its reconcile: the first reconcile must CREATE the default `PtpOperatorConfig` CR, but `config/webhook/manifests.yaml` registers the `ptpconfig-validating-webhook-configuration` webhook for `ptpoperatorconfigs` resources with `failurePolicy: Fail`. The 400-second wait expired before the bootstrap completed. -

The `gather-audit-logs` post-step (a CI framework step, not PTP operator code) attempted to collect audit logs after tests completed, but the cluster's API server at `10.8.34.117:6443` was already unreachable with repeated `i/o timeout` errors. `finished.json` confirms `"passed":true,"result":"SUCCESS"` for the actual PTP test step. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** Unknown — no code regression; this is a cluster/network infrastructure event occurring in the post phase after tests succeeded. - **Source File:** https://steps.ci.openshift.org/reference/gather-audit-logs (CI framework step, not in ptp-operator source) - **Is it a flake?** yes — transient cluster network failure in post-step log collection; the PTP tests themselves passed cleanly. - **Suggested Fix:** Retry the job. If recurrent, investigate whether the test cluster is becoming unhealthy (API server crashing or network partitioned) near job end; consider adding a timeout guard or skipping post-collection if the API server is already unreachable. --- **Relation Between Failures:** There is only one logical failure: the `gather-audit-logs` CI post-step could not reach the cluster API server (`dial tcp 10.8.34.117:6443: i/o timeout`), causing the overall job to be marked failed. This cascaded into the `Run multi-stage test post phase` failure.
